Rational Sciences are Innate, Not Dependent on Logical Standards
Ibn Taymiyya argues definition is a conventional art, not a real science, and rational sciences are innate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Ibn Taymiyya's argument that rational sciences are known through innate disposition (fitra) and do not require a conventional standard like logic.

Core Idea
Rational sciences are innate, created by Allah — logic cannot be their standard.

After dismissing the art of definition as a false convention, Ibn Taymiyya turns to the logicians' claim that logic is the standard (mizan) for rational sciences, comparable to prosody for poetry or grammar for language. He powerfully rejects this analogy, arguing that rational sciences are known by innate means that Allah has placed in humans. In this lesson, we will unpack his crucial distinction between conventional arts and innate knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the analogy being refuted
The logicians compare logic to prosody for poetry and grammar for language. Ibn Taymiyya references this to set up his refutation. Find the analogy in the passage.
Look for: 'كما أن «العَرُوض ميزان الشعر، و «النحو» و«التصريف» ميزانُ الألفاظ العربية'.
2
Extract Ibn Taymiyya's counterclaim
He states that rational sciences are known by what Allah has created in humans (fitra), not by a conventional standard.
He says: 'فإن العلوم العقلية تُعلم بما فَطَر الله عليه بني آدم من أسباب الإدراك'.
3
Understand the basis of fitra
Ibn Taymiyya gives examples of innate knowledge: knowing that something is alive, knowing, powerful, etc. This knowledge is not from convention but from Allah's creation.
He says: 'فالعلم بأن الشيء حيُّ، أو عالم، أو قادر... ليس هو من الصناعات الوضعية، بل هو من الأمور الحقيقية الفطرية'.
4
Contrast with conventional sciences
He contrasts Arabic grammar, which is learned by hearing and induction, with rational sciences that are known by fitra and not dependent on custom.
He says: 'بخلاف العربية، فإنها عادة لقوم لا تُعْرَف إلا بالسماع، وقوانينها لا تعرف إلا بالاستقراء'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صناعة الحد وضع اصطلاحي غيرُ فطري وقوله «رعاية الترتيب في هذه الأمور شرط للوفاء بصناعة الحد، وهو في غاية العُسر»، فيقال : ذلك هذه صناعة وضعيّة اصطلاحية، ليست من الأمور الحقيقية العلمية. وهي مع مخالفة لصريح العقل ولما عليه الوجود في مواضع فتكون باطلة، ليست من الأوضاع المجرَّدة كوضع أسماء الأعلام؛ فإن تلك فيها منفعة، لا تخالف عقلاً ولا وجوداً. وأما وضعهم فمخالف لصريح العقل والوجود، ولو كان وضعاً مجرّداً لم يكن ميزاناً للعلوم والحقائق فإن الأمور الحقيقية العلمية لا تختلف باختلاف الأوضاع والاصطلاحات كالمعرفة بصفات الأشياء وحقائقها. فالعلم بأن الشيء حيُّ، أو عالم، أو قادر أو مُريد أو متحرك، أو ساكن، أو حسّاس، أو غير حسّاس، ليس هو من الصناعات الوضعية، بل هو من الأمور الحقيقية الفطرية التي فطَرَ الله تعالى عباده عليها ، كما فَطَرهم على أنواع الإرادات الصحيحة والحركات المستقيمة. (1) لا سيما وهؤلاء يقولون : إن المنطق ميزان العلوم العقلية»، ومراعاتُه تَعْصِم الذهن عن أن يغلط في فكره ، كما أن «العَرُوض ميزان الشعر، و «النحو» و«التصريف» ميزانُ الألفاظ العربية - المركبة والمفردة وآلاتُ المواقيت موازين لها . العلوم العقلية ولكن ليس الأمر كذلك، فإن العلوم العقلية تُعلم بما فَطَر الله عليه بني آدم من أسباب الإدراك، لا تقف على ميزان وضعي لشخص معين، ولا يُقلد في/ «العقليات» تعلم بالفطرة أحد؛ بخلاف العربية، فإنها عادة لقوم لا تُعْرَف إلا بالسماع، وقوانينها لا تعرف إلا بالاستقراء؛ بخلاف ما به يُعرف مقادير المَكِيلات، والمَوْزونات، والمذروعات،
The art of definition is a conventional, non-innate invention. And his statement: 'Observing order in these matters is a condition for fulfilling the art of definition, and it is extremely difficult' — so it is said: This is a conventional, invented art, not among the real scientific matters. And it, while contradicting clear reason and what existence is upon in many places, is false. It is not like the purely conventional matters such as giving proper names, for those have benefit and do not contradict reason or existence. But their convention contradicts clear reason and existence. Even if it were a mere convention, it would not be a standard for sciences and realities, for real scientific matters do not differ with differences of conventions and terminologies, like knowledge of the attributes of things and their realities. So knowledge that a thing is alive, or knowing, or powerful, or willing, or moving, or stationary, or sensitive, or not sensitive — this is not among the conventional arts, but rather among the real innate matters that Allah has created His servants upon, just as He created them upon types of correct desires and upright movements. (1) Especially since these people say: 'Logic is the standard of rational sciences, and observing it safeguards the mind from error in its thinking,' just as prosody is the standard of poetry, and grammar and morphology are the standards of Arabic words — compound and singular — and timekeeping instruments are standards for them. But it is not so; for rational sciences are known by what Allah has created the children of Adam upon from means of perception; they do not depend on a conventional standard for a specific person, nor is anyone imitated in intellectual matters learned by innate disposition. Unlike Arabic, for it is a custom of a people and is only known by hearing, and its laws are only known by induction; unlike how measures, weights, and lengths are known.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a sharp critique of the logicians' claim that the art of definition (sina'at al-hadd) and logic in general are essential for rational knowledge. Ibn Taymiyya begins by asserting that the art of definition is a conventional (wad'i) and invented (istilahi) art, not a real scientific matter. He refers to al-Ghazali's statement that observing order in definitions is a condition and is extremely difficult. Ibn Taymiyya responds that this art contradicts clear reason and the nature of existence, making it false. He distinguishes it from purely conventional matters like naming, which have benefit and do not contradict reason or existence. The logicians' convention, however, does contradict both. Even if it were a mere convention, it would not serve as a standard for sciences and realities, because real scientific knowledge—such as knowing that something is alive, knowing, powerful, etc.—does not change with conventions. Such knowledge is innate (fitri), placed by Allah in His servants. Ibn Taymiyya then addresses the logicians' claim that logic is the standard of rational sciences, comparing it to prosody for poetry or grammar for language. He rejects this analogy entirely: rational sciences are known through the innate means of perception that Allah has given humans; they do not require a conventional standard. Unlike Arabic, which is a custom learned by hearing and induction, rational knowledge is innate and not subject to imitation or convention. Thus, the logicians' framework is fundamentally misguided.

Key Terms
ميزان العلوم العقلية
فطرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Ibn Taymiyya reject the logicians' claim that logic is the standard (mizan) for rational sciences?
A) Because logic is too difficult to learn.
B) Because rational sciences are known by innate disposition, not by a conventional standard.
C) Because the logicians' rules are all false.
D) Because grammarians already have a better standard.

Key Takeaway
Rational sciences are innate, known through the fitra that Allah created in humans, and therefore do not require a conventional logical standard.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Reflect on a rational principle (e.g., 'the whole is greater than the part'). Explain whether, according to Ibn Taymiyya, this is known through fitra or through logicians' conventions. Justify your answer using the passage.

The Art of Definition as Conventional vs. Innate
Ibn Taymiyya argues that the art of definition is conventional, not innate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish Ibn Taymiyya's critique of the art of definition as a conventional imposition from the logicians' claim that it is an innate science.

Core Idea
Definition is a human convention, not a universal measure for truth.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya strikes at the heart of the logicians' project: the art of definition (sina'at al-hadd) is not a natural, innate discipline but a human-made convention. He argues that real knowledge of attributes like 'living' or 'knowing' is innate (fitri) and does not depend on any artificial definitional framework. The logicians' claim that observing order in definition is necessary but difficult is met with the response that their entire art is a conventional imposition that contradicts reason and existence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two opposing positions
Locate in the Arabic where Ibn Taymiyya states that the art of definition is a conventional imposition (wad' ishtilahi) versus the logicians' claim that it is a rigorous science. Note the contrast.
2
Ibn Taymiyya's distinction between conventions
He separates pure conventions, like naming proper nouns, which are beneficial and do not contradict reason or existence, from the logicians' convention, which he says does contradict clear reason and existence.
3
Analyze why the logicians' convention fails
According to Ibn Taymiyya, even if it were a pure convention, it could not serve as a measure for sciences and truths because real scientific matters (like knowing that something is alive) are innate and do not vary with conventions.
He gives examples: knowing something is alive, knowing, powerful, etc.
4
Understand the fitra argument
Ibn Taymiyya emphasizes that knowledge of the attributes of things is among the real innate matters (umur haqiqiyya fitriyya) that God has created people upon. This is the foundation of our cognition, not any conventional definitional system.
This is a key epistemological point: fitra is the source of certain knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صناعة الحد وضع اصطلاحي غيرُ فِطري
وقوله «رعاية الترتيب في هذه الأمور شرط للوفاء بصناعة الحد، وهو في غاية العُسر»، فيقال : ذلك هذه صناعة وضعيّة اصطلاحية، ليست من الأمور الحقيقية العلمية. وهي مع مخالفة لصريح العقل ولما عليه الوجود في مواضع فتكون باطلة، ليست من الأوضاع المجرَّدة كوضع أسماء الأعلام؛ فإن تلك فيها منفعة، لا تخالف عقلاً ولا وجوداً. وأما وضعهم فمخالف لصريح العقل والوجود، ولو كان وضعاً مجرّداً لم يكن ميزاناً للعلوم والحقائق فإن الأمور الحقيقية العلمية لا تختلف باختلاف الأوضاع والاصطلاحات كالمعرفة بصفات الأشياء وحقائقها. فالعلم بأن الشيء حيُّ، أو عالم، أو قادر أو مُريد أو متحرك، أو ساكن، أو حسّاس، أو غير حسّاس، ليس هو من الصناعات الوضعية، بل هو من الأمور الحقيقية الفطرية التي فطَرَ الله تعالى عباده عليها ، كما فَطَرهم على أنواع الإرادات الصحيحة والحركات المستقيمة. لا سيما وهؤلاء يقولون : إن المنطق ميزان العلوم العقلية»، ومراعاتُه تَعْصِم الذهن عن أن يغلط في فكره ، كما أن «العَرُوض ميزان الشعر، و «النحو» و«التصريف» ميزانُ الألفاظ العربية - المركبة والمفردة وآلاتُ المواقيت موازين لها . العلوم العقلية ولكن ليس الأمر كذلك، فإن العلوم العقلية تُعلم بما فَطَر الله عليه بني آدم من أسباب الإدراك، لا تقف على ميزان وضعي لشخص معين، ولا يُقلد في/ «العقليات» تعلم بالفطرة أحد؛ بخلاف العربية، فإنها عادة لقوم لا تُعْرَف إلا بالسماع، وقوانينها لا تعرف إلا بالاستقراء؛ بخلاف ما به يُعرف مقادير المَكِيلات، والمَوْزونات، والمذروعات، والمَعْدُودات، فإنها تفتقر إلى ذلك غالباً. لكن تعيين ما به يكال ويوزن بقدر مخصوص أمر عادي كعادة الناس في اللغات. وقد تنازع علماء المسلمين في مسمَّى «الدرهم» و«الدينار»، هل هو مقدر بالشرع، أو المرجع فيه إلى العُزف على قولين أصحهما الثاني. وعلى ذلك يبنى النصاب الشرعي، هل هو مئتا در هم بوزن معين أو مئتا درهم مما يتعامل بها الناس و اعتبار تقديرها
The art of definition is a conventional imposition, not innate. And his statement: 'Observing order in these matters is a condition for fulfilling the art of definition, and it is extremely difficult.' So it is said: That is a conventional, conventional art, not a real scientific matter. And it, while contradicting clear reason and what existence is upon in places, is false. It is not among pure conventions like naming proper nouns; for those have benefit, not contradicting reason or existence. But their convention contradicts clear reason and existence. And if it were a pure convention, it would not be a measure for sciences and truths, for real scientific matters do not differ with differences in conventions and terminologies, like knowledge of the attributes of things and their realities. So knowledge that a thing is alive, or knowing, or powerful, or willing, or moving, or stationary, or sensory, or non-sensory, is not among conventional arts, but rather among real innate matters that God Almighty has created His servants upon, just as He created them upon types of correct wills and straight movements. Especially since these people say that logic is the measure of rational sciences, and its observance protects the mind from error in its thinking, just as prosody is the measure of poetry, and grammar and morphology are the measure of Arabic words—compound and single—and instruments of timings are measures for them. But it is not so, for rational sciences are known by what God has created upon the children of Adam of means of perception; they do not depend on a conventional measure for a specific person, nor is anyone imitated in rational matters taught by innate disposition. Unlike Arabic, for it is a custom of a people not known except by hearing, and its rules are not known except by induction. Unlike what is known of measures of solids, weights, lengths, and counts, for these mostly depend on that. But specifying what is measured and weighed by a specific quantity is a customary matter like the custom of people in languages. And the Muslim scholars have disputed concerning the name 'dirham' and 'dinar': is it legally determined, or is reference made to custom? There are two opinions, the more correct of which is the second. And upon this is built the legal threshold: is it two hundred dirhams of a specific weight, or two hundred dirhams of what people transact with, and consideration of its evaluation?
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a critical argument. Ibn Taymiyya begins by stating that the art of definition (sina'at al-hadd) is a conventional imposition (wad' ishtilahi), not an innate (fitri) matter. He then quotes an opponent who claims that observing order in definition is necessary but difficult. Ibn Taymiyya responds that this art is conventional and not based on real scientific truths; moreover, it contradicts reason and reality in some respects, making it invalid. He distinguishes between pure conventions like naming proper nouns (which are beneficial and non-contradictory) and the logicians' convention, which contradicts reason and existence. Even if it were a pure convention, it could not serve as a measure for sciences and truths, because real scientific knowledge (e.g., knowing that something is alive or knowing) is innate and does not change with conventions. Ibn Taymiyya then attacks the logicians' claim that logic is a measure for rational sciences, comparing it to prosody for poetry or grammar for Arabic. He argues that rational sciences are known through innate disposition (fitra) and do not require a conventional measure. In contrast, Arabic and weights/measures are conventional and require hearing or induction. He gives an example from Islamic jurisprudence: the disagreement over whether the dirham and dinar are legally determined (shar'an) or based on custom ('urf). The correct opinion, he says, is that reference is to custom. This illustrates that conventional measures are not fixed by revelation but by societal norms.

Key Terms
صناعة الحد
وضع اصطلاحي
فطري
ميزان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, what makes the art of definition invalid as a measure for sciences?
A) It is too difficult to learn.
B) It is a conventional art that contradicts reason and existence.
C) It was invented by non-Muslims.
D) It is not mentioned in the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The art of definition is a human convention that cannot serve as a universal measure for knowledge; true knowledge is innate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Using Ibn Taymiyya's framework, explain why the knowledge that 'the world is created' is an innate truth (fitri) rather than a result of the logicians' art of definition.

Logic as a Measure for Rational Sciences - Refutation
Ibn Taymiyya refutes logic as a measure for rational sciences using a fiqh example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's argument that logic cannot serve as a universal measure for rational sciences and identify the fiqh example he uses to support his view.

Core Idea
Logic is like prosody: conventional, not universal; rational sciences rely on fitra.

Ibn Taymiyya directly challenges the logicians' claim that logic is the 'measure' (mizan) for rational sciences, similar to prosody for poetry or grammar for Arabic. He argues that rational sciences are known by innate disposition, not by any conventional measure. To illustrate his point, he gives an example from Islamic jurisprudence: the dispute over whether the dirham and dinar are legally determined or based on custom. This example shows that even in legal matters, conventions are based on custom, not fixed by revelation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the logicians' analogy
Find in the Arabic where Ibn Taymiyya quotes the logicians' claim: logic is a measure for rational sciences just as prosody is for poetry and grammar for Arabic. Note the terms 'mizan' and 'arud' etc.
2
Ibn Taymiyya's rejection of the analogy
He says 'but it is not so' (wa lakin laysa al-amr kadhalik). Rational sciences are known by what God has created in humans as means of perception, not by a conventional measure.
He emphasizes that rational sciences do not depend on a conventional measure for a specific person.
3
Distinction between conventional and innate knowledge
Arabic (grammar, prosody) is a custom of a people, learned by hearing and induction. Measures of solids, weights, etc., are conventional and depend on specific quantities. But rational truths are innate and universal.
4
Analyze the fiqh example
Ibn Taymiyya cites the dispute among Muslim scholars about the dirham and dinar: are they legally determined (shar'an) or based on custom ('urf)? He says the more correct opinion is that reference is to custom. This shows that even in sacred law, conventional measures are not fixed by revelation but by societal norms.
This example is used to support his argument that logic is a similar conventional measure, not a universal truth.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

He then quotes an opponent who claims that observing order in definition is necessary but difficult. Ibn Taymiyya responds that this art is conventional and not based on real scientific truths; moreover, it contradicts reason and reality in some respects, making it invalid. He distinguishes between pure conventions like naming proper nouns (which are beneficial and non-contradictory) and the logicians' convention, which contradicts reason and existence. Even if it were a pure convention, it could not serve as a measure for sciences and truths, because real scientific knowledge (e.g., knowing that something is alive or knowing) is innate and does not change with conventions. Ibn Taymiyya then attacks the logicians' claim that logic is a measure for rational sciences, comparing it to prosody for poetry or grammar for Arabic. He argues that rational sciences are known through innate disposition (fitra) and do not require a conventional measure. In contrast, Arabic and weights/measures are conventional and require hearing or induction. He gives an example from Islamic jurisprudence: the disagreement over whether the dirham and dinar are legally determined (shar'an) or based on custom ('urf). The correct opinion, he says, is that reference is to custom. This illustrates that conventional measures are not fixed by revelation but by societal norms.

Key Terms
صناعة الحد
وضع اصطلاحي
فطري
ميزان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because logic is universal while prosody is specific to Arabic.
B) Because rational sciences are innate and do not require a conventional measure.
C) Because prosody and grammar are divinely revealed.
D) Because logic is too difficult to learn.

Key Takeaway
Logic is a conventional measure that cannot govern rational sciences because rational truths are known innately by fitra.

Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of Essential Attributes in Definition
Ibn Taymiyya analyzes the difficulty of distinguishing essential and accidental attributes in definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's objection to the logicians' definition (hadd) and distinguish it from description of the name (sharh al-ism).

Core Idea
Distinguishing essential from accidental attributes among similars is either impossible or useless.

Ibn Taymiyya launches a powerful critique against the classical logicians' project of constructing definitions based on essential attributes. He argues that the very act of separating essential from accidental traits among similar things is either impossible or yields no new knowledge. In this lesson, we will unpack his reasoning and explore his alternative: the 'description of the name' (sharh al-ism), which aims to clarify meaning without claiming to capture essences. Understanding this critique is crucial for evaluating the epistemological foundations of definitions in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the logicians' claim being attacked
The logicians assert that a true definition (hadd) must be composed of essential attributes arranged in a specific order to distinguish the essence of a thing. Ibn Taymiyya targets the feasibility of identifying those essential attributes and the necessity of that order.
2
Follow Ibn Taymiyya's deconstruction
He argues that differentiating between similar attributes (e.g., two near-identical qualities) is impossible because there is no objective criterion to deem one essential and the other accidental. If attributes are merely close but not identical, the task becomes extremely difficult. Even if one succeeds, the result provides no new knowledge beyond what was already known without the definition.
This is an epistemological argument about human inability to access essential natures.
3
Identify his alternative
Ibn Taymiyya introduces 'sharh al-ism' (description of the name) as a viable alternative. This merely clarifies what the speaker means by a term, whether that meaning corresponds to an external reality or not, without claiming to capture the essence.
4
Evaluate the critique's internal validity
The critique is logically sound: it does not rely on formal logic but on the practical impossibility of distinguishing similars. Ibn Taymiyya's own argument does not fall into the same problem because he is not defining a term by essential attributes; he is describing a process.
The critique itself is a meta-level analysis, not a definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولما راموا ذلك لم يكن بد من أن يفرّقوا بين بعض الصفات وبعض، إذ جعلوا التفريق التصور بما جعلوه ذاتياً، فلا بد أن يفرقوا بين ما هو ذاتي عندهم وما ليس كذلك، ولا بد أن يرتبوا ذكرها على ترتيب مخصوص إذ لا تذكر على كل ترتيب. فكانت الصفات الذاتية مادة الحد الوضعي، والترتيب الذي ذكروه هو صورته. ولما كان ذلك مستلزماً للتفريق بين المتماثلين أو المتقاربين كان ممتنعاً أو عسيراً، إذ يفرقون بين صفة وصفة بجعل إحداهما ذاتية دون أخرى مع تساويهما أو تقاربهما، ويفرقون بين ترتيب وترتيب بجعل أحدهما معرفا للحقيقة دون الآخر مع تساويهما أو تقاربهما. وطلب الفرق بين المتماثلات طلب ما لا حقيقة له فهو ممتنع؛ وإن كان بين المتقاربين كان عسيراً. فالمطلوب إما متعذراً وإما متعسراً. فإن كان متعذراً بطل بالكلية، وإن كان متعسراً فهو بعد حصوله ليس فيه فائدة زائدة على ما كان يعرف قبل حصوله. فصاروا بين أن يمتنع عليهم ما شرطوه أو ينالوه ولا يحصل به ما قصدوه. وعلى التقديرين ليس ما وضعوه من الحد طريقاً لتصور الحقائق في نفس من لا يتصورها بدون الحد، وإن كان الحد قد يفيد من تنبيه المخاطب وتمييز المحدود ما قد تفيده الأسماء، كما سيأتي بيانه إن شاء الله تعالى. وما ذكروه من الفرق بين الحد وشرح الاسم فتلخيصه أن المحدود المميز عن غيره إذا تصورت حقيقته فقد يكون هو الموجود الخارجي، وقد يكون هو المراد الذهني، وشرح الاسم فقد يراد بالحد تمييز ما عناه المتكلم بالاسم وتفهيمه، سواء كان ذلك المعنى الذي أراده بالاسم ثابتاً في الخارج أو لم يكن. وقد يراد به تمييز ما هو موجود في الخارج.
And when they attempted that, they had to differentiate between some attributes and others, as they made the differentiation of concepts by what they made essential. Thus they had to differentiate between what is essential according to them and what is not, and they had to arrange their mention in a specific order, since they are not mentioned in every order. So the essential attributes became the matter of the conventional definition, and the order they mentioned is its form. And since this necessitated differentiation between similars or near-similars, it became impossible or difficult. For they differentiate between one attribute and another by making one essential and another not, despite their equality or proximity; and they differentiate between one order and another by making one a definer of the reality and another not, despite their equality or proximity. And seeking differentiation between similars is seeking what has no reality, so it is impossible; if it is between near-similars, it is difficult. So the required thing is either impossible or very difficult. If it is impossible, it is nullified entirely; if it is very difficult, then after attaining it there is no additional benefit beyond what was known before attaining it. Thus they end up either unable to achieve what they stipulated, or they achieve it but do not obtain what they intended. In both cases, what they established of definition is not a path to conceptualize realities in the mind of one who does not conceptualize them without the definition, even if the definition may sometimes benefit in alerting the addressee and distinguishing the defined as names may do, as will be explained if God wills. And what they mentioned of the difference between definition (hadd) and description of the name (sharh al-ism), its summary is that the defined that distinguishes from others when its reality is conceptualized may be the external existent or the mental referent; and description of the name may intend by the definition to distinguish what the speaker meant by the name and to make it understood, whether that meaning he intended by the name exists externally or not; and it may intend to distinguish what exists externally.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is a critical analysis of the logicians' project of constructing definitions (hadd) based on essential attributes. Ibn Taymiyya argues that the logicians require distinguishing essential from accidental attributes, and arranging them in a specific order. However, differentiating between two similar attributes is impossible, and between near-similar attributes is very difficult. Even if they succeed, the result provides no new knowledge. He also addresses the distinction between 'hadd' (definition of the essence) and 'sharh al-ism' (description of the name). The former aims to define the external reality, while the latter aims to clarify the speaker's meaning, regardless of external existence. Ibn Taymiyya concludes that their definition does not help one who does not already know the reality.

ذاتي

B) It is too simple.

D) It is impossible to write.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya shows that the logicians' definition (hadd) is either impossible or useless; a more viable alternative is the description of the name (sharh al-ism).

Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of Essential Attributes in Definitions
Ibn Taymiyya critiques the logicians' attempt to distinguish essential from accidental attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's argument against the logicians' use of essential attributes and evaluate its validity.

Core Idea
Essential attributes are arbitrary; definitions based on them are either impossible or useless.

Ibn Taymiyya challenges the very foundation of logical definitions: the idea that some attributes are 'essential' and others accidental. In this passage, he exposes the practical impossibility of consistently distinguishing between similar attributes, and questions the benefit even if such a distinction were possible. This lesson will help you understand his critique and apply it to Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the logicians' claim being attacked
The logicians claim that definitions (hadd) must consist of essential attributes (dhati) arranged in a specific order. Ibn Taymiyya targets this requirement.
Essential attributes are those that constitute the essence of a thing; accidental attributes are additional.
2
Understand the basis of the requirement
The logicians need to differentiate between essential and accidental attributes, and also order them properly. This is the 'matter' and 'form' of the definition.
Ibn Taymiyya calls this 'al-hadd al-wad'i'.
3
Follow Ibn Taymiyya's deconstruction
He argues that attributes are often similar or close, making it impossible to distinguish which is essential and which is not. If they are perfectly similar, the distinction is impossible; if only close, it is difficult and yields no new knowledge.
This is the core of his critique: the task is either impossible or futile.
4
Evaluate the consequence
If the distinction is impossible, the whole project collapses. If it is difficult and useless, then it fails to achieve its purpose of providing certain knowledge.
Ibn Taymiyya concludes that the logicians are between a rock and a hard place.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولما راموا ذلك لم يكن بد من أن يفرّقوا بين بعض الصفات وبعض، إذ جعلوا التفريق التصوّر بما جعلوه ذاتياً، فلا بد أن يفرقوا بين ما هو ذاتي عندهم وما ليس كذلك، ولا بد أن يرتبوا ذكرها على ترتيب مخصوص إذ لا تُذكر على كل ترتيب. فكانت الصفات الذاتية مادة الحدّ الوضعي، والترتيب الذي ذكروه هو «صورته». ولما كان ذلك مستلزماً للتفريق بين المتماثلين أو المتقاربين كان ممتنعاً أو عسيراً، إذ يفرقون بين صفة وصفة بجعل إحداهما «ذاتية» دون أخرى مع تساويهما أو تقاربهما، ويفرّقون بين ترتيب وترتيب بجعل أحدهما معرّفاً للحقيقة دون الآخر مع تساويهما أو تقاربهما. وطلبُ الفَرْقِ بين المتماثلات طلب ما لا حقيقة له فهو ممتنع؛ وإن كان بين المتقاربين كان عَسِراً. فالمطلوب إما متعذراً وإما متعسّراً. فإن كان متعذراً بَطَل بالكلية، وإن كان متعسّراً فهو بعد حصوله ليس فيه فائدة زائدة على ما كان يُعرَف قبل حصوله. فصاروا بين أن يمتنع عليهم ما شَرَطوه أو ينالوه ولا يحصل به ما قصدوه.
When they aimed at that, it was necessary for them to differentiate between some attributes and others, since they made differentiation of conceptualization by what they considered essential. So they must distinguish between what is essential according to them and what is not, and they must arrange their mention in a specific order since they are not mentioned in every order. Thus, the essential attributes are the matter of the conventional definition (al-hadd al-wad'i), and the order they mentioned is its 'form'. Since that necessitated differentiation between similar or close things, it became impossible or difficult, for they differentiate between one attribute and another by making one 'essential' without another while they are equal or close, and they differentiate between one order and another by making one a definer of the reality without the other while they are equal or close. Seeking the difference between similar things is seeking what has no reality, so it is impossible; if between close things, it is difficult. So the sought thing is either impossible or difficult. If it is impossible, it is utterly invalid; if it is difficult, then after attaining it, there is no additional benefit beyond what was known before attaining it. Thus, they are between making impossible what they stipulated or attaining it without achieving what they intended.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage critiques the logicians' project of defining things through essential attributes arranged in a specific order. Ibn Taymiyya argues that the distinction between essential and accidental attributes is arbitrary because attributes often resemble each other. He points out that even if a distinction were possible, it adds no new knowledge beyond what was already known. The passage exposes the futility of the logicians' method: either the distinction is impossible, making the entire endeavor invalid, or it is difficult and yields no benefit.

الحد الوضعي
المتماثلين

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya exposes the arbitrary nature of essential attributes, showing that the logician's definitional project is either impossible or useless.

Distinction Between Hadd and Sharh al-Ism
Ibn Taymiyya distinguishes two senses of definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between definition that clarifies the speaker's intended meaning (sharh al-ism) and definition that describes external reality.

Core Idea
Definition can explain a word without describing external reality.

Ibn Taymiyya clarifies that the term 'definition' (hadd) is used in two distinct senses: one as an explanation of the name (sharh al-ism), which simply clarifies what the speaker means, and another as a description of the existent, which aims to correspond to external reality. This distinction is crucial for avoiding confusion in scholarly debates.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two purposes
In the passage, find where Ibn Taymiyya says definition may be intended to distinguish the speaker's intended meaning or to distinguish what exists externally. Note that the first does not require external truth.
2
Understand the condition of sharh al-ism
Shrah al-ism only clarifies what the speaker means, regardless of whether that meaning corresponds to external reality. The listener may not need to check correspondence.
3
Compare with descriptive definition
The second type of definition aims to match external reality. If the definition does not correspond, it is false, not just unclear.
4
Apply the distinction
Consider how this distinction resolves misunderstandings: a listener may think the speaker's definition is false when it is only explanatory, or vice versa.
The passage gives the example of someone thinking the explainer did not understand due to difficulty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما ذكروه من الفرق بين الحدّ وشرح الاسم فتلخيصه أن المحدود المميز عن غيره إذا تُصوِّرت حقيقته فقد يكون هو الموجود الخارجي، وقد يكون هو المراد الذهني، وشرح الاسم فقد يُراد بالحدّ تمييزُ ما عَناه المتكلم بالاسم وتفهيمه، سواء كان ذلك المعنى الذي أراده بالاسم ثابتاً في الخارج أو لم يكن. وقد يُراد به تمييز ما هو موجود في الخارج. وهذا شأن كل من فسّر كلام متكلم أو شَرَحه، فقد يفسّر مراد المتكلم ومقصوده، سواء كان مطابقاً للخارج أو لم يكن، وقد يتبين مع ذلك أنه مطابق للأمر الخارج، وأنه حق في نفسه. وإذا كان الكلام غير حق لم يكن مطابقاً للخارج فيريد المستمع أن يطابق بينه وبين الواقع فلا يطابقه ولا يوافقه حتى قد يظن الظان أن الشارح أو المستمع لم يفهم مقصود المتكلم لِعُسْرته، ولا يكون كذلك، بل لأن ما ذكره من الكلام ليس بمطابق للواقع فلا يمكن مطابقته إياه. وقد يكون ظنُّ من ظنّه مطابقاً للخارج إحساناً للظن بالمتكلم؛ ويكون قد ظنّ أنه لم يفهمه لدقته عليه فلا يكون كذلك. هذا وقولهم في الحدّ الحقيقي: إنه متعسّر، وإنه لا يقف عليه إلا آحاد الناس هو من الباب. فإن الحدّ الحقيقي إذا أريد به ما زعموه فإنه لا حقيقة له في الخارج، إذ يريدون به أن الموصوف في نفسه مؤلف من بعض صفاته اللازمة له التي بعضُها أعم منه وبعضُها مطابق له دون بعض صفاته اللازمة المساوية لتلك العامة في العموم وللمطابقة في المطابقة دون بعض، وأن حقيقته هي مركبة من تلك الصفات دون غيرها، وأن تلك الحقيقة يصورها الحد دون غيره. فهذا ليس بحق. فدعواهم تأليفه من بعض الصفات اللازمة دون بعض باطلة، بل دعواهم أنه مركب من الصفات باطلة ودعواهم له حقيقة ثابتة في الخارج يصورها الحدّ دون غيره باطلة. وإنما الواقع أن المحدود الموصوف الذي ميّز بالاسم أو الحدّ عن غيره قد يكون ثابتاً في الخارج، وقد يكون ثابتاً في المتكلم بالاسم أو الحد وهو يظن ثبوته في الخارج وليس كذلك. ولهذا يقال: الحد يكون تارةً بحسب الاسم، وتارةً بحسب المسمى ويقال: «الحد يكون تارةً بحسب اسم الشيء، وتارة بحسب حقيقته. وإن كان الحد بحسب الاسم قد يكون مطابقاً للخارج، لكن المقصود أن الحد تارةً يميز بين المراد باللفظ وغير المراد، وتارة يميز بين الموجود في الخارج من الأعيان وبين غيره؛ وهذا التمييز إنما يحصل بواسطة ذلك. فالتمييز الذي في النفس يجب أن يكون مطابقاً للتمييز في الخارج، والتمييز الذي يحصل للمستمع هو بواسطة التمييز الذي في نفس المتكلم، والله أعلم.
And what they mentioned regarding the distinction between definition (hadd) and explanation of the name (sharh al-ism): its summary is that the defined thing distinguished from others, if its reality is conceptualized, may be the external existent or the mental intended meaning. Explanation of the name: definition may be intended to distinguish what the speaker meant by the name and to make it understood, whether that meaning which he intended by the name is established externally or not. And it may be intended to distinguish what exists externally. This is the case with everyone who interprets the speech of a speaker or explains it; he may explain the speaker's intent and purpose, whether it corresponds to external reality or not, and it may become clear along with that that it corresponds to the external matter and that it is true in itself. If the speech is not true, it does not correspond to the external, so the listener wants to match it with reality but it does not match nor correspond, so much so that one may think that the explainer or listener did not understand the speaker's intent due to its difficulty, but it is not so; rather, because the speech mentioned does not correspond to reality, it is impossible to match it to it. And sometimes the one who thinks it corresponds to the external is being charitable in his assumption about the speaker; and he may have thought that he did not understand it due to its subtlety, but it is not so. This, and their statement about real definition (al-hadd al-haqiqi): that it is difficult, and that only a few people grasp it, is of the same kind. For real definition, if intended as they claim, has no reality in the external, since they intend by it that the described thing in itself is composed of some of its necessary attributes, some of which are more general than it and some are coextensive with it, to the exclusion of other necessary attributes that are equal to those general ones in generality and to those coextensive ones in coextension, and that its reality is composed of those attributes and not others, and that definition depicts that reality to the exclusion of others. This is not true. So their claim that it is composed of some necessary attributes and not others is false; rather, their claim that it is composed of attributes is false, and their claim that it has a fixed reality in the external that definition depicts to the exclusion of others is false. The reality is that the defined described thing, distinguished by name or definition from others, may be established externally, or may be established in the speaker of the name or definition while he thinks it is external but it is not. For this reason, it is said: definition is sometimes according to the name, and sometimes according to the named. And it is said: 'Definition is sometimes according to the name of the thing, and sometimes according to its reality.' Even if definition according to the name may correspond to the external, the point is that definition sometimes distinguishes between what is intended by the utterance and what is not, and sometimes distinguishes between what exists externally in concrete entities and what is not; this distinction only occurs by means of that. So the distinction in the mind must correspond to the distinction in the external, and the distinction that occurs to the listener is by means of the distinction in the speaker's mind. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage elaborates the distinction between definition (hadd) and explanation of the name (sharh al-ism), then critiques the logicians' notion of real definition (al-hadd al-haqiqi). Ibn Taymiyya explains that definition can serve two purposes: clarifying the speaker's intended meaning (regardless of external existence) or describing what exists in the external world. He notes that the logicians claim real definition is difficult and rare, but he argues that their concept of real definition—as a composition of specific necessary attributes that capture the essence to the exclusion of others—has no basis in reality. He asserts that the claim that things are composed of attributes is itself false, let alone the selection of some attributes over others. Ultimately, definition is merely a tool for distinguishing meanings, not a revelation of essences. The passage emphasizes that any mental distinction must correspond to an external distinction to be true; otherwise, the definition is only explanatory of the speaker's intention.

Key Terms
الحد
شرح الاسم
الحد الحقيقي

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The first clarifies the speaker's intention regardless of external existence; the second aims to describe what exists externally.
C) The first is only for physical objects; the second for abstract concepts.
D) There is no difference; they are the same.

Key Takeaway
Definition can merely explain a term without describing external reality.

Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of Real Definition
Ibn Taymiyya critiques the logicians' real definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's argument that the logicians' real definition (al-hadd al-haqiqi) has no basis in external reality.

Core Idea
The logicians' claim that definitions capture essences is baseless; only mental distinctions exist.

Having distinguished the two senses of definition, Ibn Taymiyya turns to the logicians' notion of real definition—a definition that supposedly reveals the true essence of a thing. He argues that this concept is fundamentally flawed because it assumes things are composed of attributes, which is false, and that such a definition has no external reality.

Guided Path
1
State the logicians' claim
The logicians claim that real definition is a combination of necessary attributes that depict the essence of a thing, and that it is difficult to attain.
2
Identify Ibn Taymiyya's first refutation
He argues that the claim that a thing is composed of some necessary attributes and not others is arbitrary and false.
3
Identify his second refutation
The very idea that a thing is composed of attributes at all is false. Attributes are not parts of the thing; they are predicated of it.
4
Identify his third refutation
Even if composition were accepted, there is no fixed external reality that definition uniquely depicts. The defined thing may or may not exist externally.
5
Understand the alternative
Ibn Taymiyya concludes that definition is merely a tool for distinguishing meanings, not a revelation of essences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما ذكروه من الفرق بين الحدّ وشرح الاسم فتلخيصه أن المحدود المميز عن غيره إذا تُصوِّرت حقيقته فقد يكون هو الموجود الخارجي، وقد يكون هو المراد الذهني، وشرح الاسم فقد يُراد بالحدّ تمييزُ ما عَناه المتكلم بالاسم وتفهيمه، سواء كان ذلك المعنى الذي أراده بالاسم ثابتاً في الخارج أو لم يكن. وقد يُراد به تمييز ما هو موجود في الخارج. وهذا شأن كل من فسّر كلام متكلم أو شَرَحه، فقد يفسّر مراد المتكلم ومقصوده، سواء كان مطابقاً للخارج أو لم يكن، وقد يتبين مع ذلك أنه مطابق للأمر الخارج، وأنه حق في نفسه. وإذا كان الكلام غير حق لم يكن مطابقاً للخارج فيريد المستمع أن يطابق بينه وبين الواقع فلا يطابقه ولا يوافقه حتى قد يظن الظان أن الشارح أو المستمع لم يفهم مقصود المتكلم لِعُسْرته، ولا يكون كذلك، بل لأن ما ذكره من الكلام ليس بمطابق للواقع فلا يمكن مطابقته إياه. وقد يكون ظنُّ من ظنّه مطابقاً للخارج إحساناً للظن بالمتكلم؛ ويكون قد ظنّ أنه لم يفهمه لدقته عليه فلا يكون كذلك. هذا وقولهم في الحدّ الحقيقي: إنه متعسّر، وإنه لا يقف عليه إلا آحاد الناس هو من الباب. فإن الحدّ الحقيقي إذا أريد به ما زعموه فإنه لا حقيقة له في الخارج، إذ يريدون به أن الموصوف في نفسه مؤلف من بعض صفاته اللازمة له التي بعضُها أعم منه وبعضُها مطابق له دون بعض صفاته اللازمة المساوية لتلك العامة في العموم وللمطابقة في المطابقة دون بعض، وأن حقيقته هي مركبة من تلك الصفات دون غيرها، وأن تلك الحقيقة يصورها الحد دون غيره. فهذا ليس بحق. فدعواهم تأليفه من بعض الصفات اللازمة دون بعض باطلة، بل دعواهم أنه مركب من الصفات باطلة ودعواهم له حقيقة ثابتة في الخارج يصورها الحدّ دون غيره باطلة. وإنما الواقع أن المحدود الموصوف الذي ميّز بالاسم أو الحدّ عن غيره قد يكون ثابتاً في الخارج، وقد يكون ثابتاً في المتكلم بالاسم أو الحد وهو يظن ثبوته في الخارج وليس كذلك. ولهذا يقال: الحد يكون تارةً بحسب الاسم، وتارةً بحسب المسمى ويقال: «الحد يكون تارةً بحسب اسم الشيء، وتارة بحسب حقيقته. وإن كان الحد بحسب الاسم قد يكون مطابقاً للخارج، لكن المقصود أن الحد تارةً يميز بين المراد باللفظ وغير المراد، وتارة يميز بين الموجود في الخارج من الأعيان وبين غيره؛ وهذا التمييز إنما يحصل بواسطة ذلك. فالتمييز الذي في النفس يجب أن يكون مطابقاً للتمييز في الخارج، والتمييز الذي يحصل للمستمع هو بواسطة التمييز الذي في نفس المتكلم، والله أعلم.
And what they mentioned regarding the distinction between definition (hadd) and explanation of the name (sharh al-ism): its summary is that the defined thing distinguished from others, if its reality is conceptualized, may be the external existent or the mental intended meaning. Explanation of the name: definition may be intended to distinguish what the speaker meant by the name and to make it understood, whether that meaning which he intended by the name is established externally or not. And it may be intended to distinguish what exists externally. This is the case with everyone who interprets the speech of a speaker or explains it; he may explain the speaker's intent and purpose, whether it corresponds to external reality or not, and it may become clear along with that that it corresponds to the external matter and that it is true in itself. If the speech is not true, it does not correspond to the external, so the listener wants to match it with reality but it does not match nor correspond, so much so that one may think that the explainer or listener did not understand the speaker's intent due to its difficulty, but it is not so; rather, because the speech mentioned does not correspond to reality, it is impossible to match it to it. And sometimes the one who thinks it corresponds to the external is being charitable in his assumption about the speaker; and he may have thought that he did not understand it due to its subtlety, but it is not so. This, and their statement about real definition (al-hadd al-haqiqi): that it is difficult, and that only a few people grasp it, is of the same kind. For real definition, if intended as they claim, has no reality in the external, since they intend by it that the described thing in itself is composed of some of its necessary attributes, some of which are more general than it and some are coextensive with it, to the exclusion of other necessary attributes that are equal to those general ones in generality and to those coextensive ones in coextension, and that its reality is composed of those attributes and not others, and that definition depicts that reality to the exclusion of others. This is not true. So their claim that it is composed of some necessary attributes and not others is false; rather, their claim that it is composed of attributes is false, and their claim that it has a fixed reality in the external that definition depicts to the exclusion of others is false. The reality is that the defined described thing, distinguished by name or definition from others, may be established externally, or may be established in the speaker of the name or definition while he thinks it is external but it is not. For this reason, it is said: definition is sometimes according to the name, and sometimes according to the named. And it is said: 'Definition is sometimes according to the name of the thing, and sometimes according to its reality.' Even if definition according to the name may correspond to the external, the point is that definition sometimes distinguishes between what is intended by the utterance and what is not, and sometimes distinguishes between what exists externally in concrete entities and what is not; this distinction only occurs by means of that. So the distinction in the mind must correspond to the distinction in the external, and the distinction that occurs to the listener is by means of the distinction in the speaker's mind. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage elaborates the distinction between definition (hadd) and explanation of the name (sharh al-ism), then critiques the logicians' notion of real definition (al-hadd al-haqiqi). Ibn Taymiyya explains that definition can serve two purposes: clarifying the speaker's intended meaning (regardless of external existence) or describing what exists in the external world. He notes that the logicians claim real definition is difficult and rare, but he argues that their concept of real definition—as a composition of specific necessary attributes that capture the essence to the exclusion of others—has no basis in reality. He asserts that the claim that things are composed of attributes is itself false, let alone the selection of some attributes over others. Ultimately, definition is merely a tool for distinguishing meanings, not a revelation of essences. The passage emphasizes that any mental distinction must correspond to an external distinction to be true; otherwise, the definition is only explanatory of the speaker's intention.

Key Terms
الحد
شرح الاسم
الحد الحقيقي

B) It assumes things are composed of attributes, which is false.

Key Takeaway
Real definition as claimed by logicians has no basis in external reality.

advanced
12 min
Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of Real Definition
Ibn Taymiyya argues that the logicians' real definition is false and impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the flaws in the logicians' concept of real definition according to Ibn Taymiyya and distinguish between definition by name and definition by named.

Core Idea
Real definition does not capture an objective essence; it is a mental distinction that may not correspond to external reality.

This passage from Ibn Taymiyya's critique targets the logicians' claim that a real definition (hadd haqiqi) depicts the true essence of a thing. Ibn Taymiyya argues that such a definition is arbitrary and has no basis in external existence. Instead, he distinguishes between definition according to the name (al-hadd bi-hasb al-ism) and definition according to the named (al-hadd bi-hasb al-musamma), emphasizing that the distinction in the mind must match external reality for knowledge to be valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem of correspondence
Ibn Taymiyya starts by discussing how interpreting speech may or may not match external reality. He emphasizes that false speech cannot be made to correspond. This sets up the issue with definitions that claim to capture reality but do not.
2
Locate the critique of real definition
Find where Ibn Taymiyya explicitly discusses 'al-hadd al-haqiqi'. He says it has no reality in external existence (la haqiqata lahu fi al-kharij). Identify his reasons: their claim of composition from some essential attributes is arbitrary and false.
3
Understand the alternative distinction
Ibn Taymiyya replaces real definition with a distinction between definition by name and definition by named. Note that definition by name distinguishes meanings, while definition by named distinguishes external entities. This shows that definitions are mental tools, not mirrors of essences.
4
Link to epistemic conditions
The passage concludes that the distinction in the mind must correspond to external distinction. This is a critical epistemological point: our mental classifications are valid only if they match reality. Ibn Taymiyya guards against the illusion that definitions alone provide objective knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شأن كل من فسّر كلام متكلم أو شرحه، فقد يفسّر مراد المتكلم ومقصوده، سواء كان مطابقاً للخارج أو لم يكن، وقد يتبين مع ذلك أنه مطابق للأمر الخارج، وأنه حق في نفسه. وإذا كان الكلام غير حق لم يكن مطابقاً للخارج فيريد المستمع أن يطابق بينه وبين الواقع فلا يطابقه ولا يوافقه حتى قد يظن الظان أن الشارح أو المستمع لم يفهم مقصود المتكلم لعسرته، ولا يكون كذلك، بل لأن ما ذكره من الكلام ليس بمطابق للواقع فلا يمكن مطابقته إياه. وقد يكون ظن من ظنه مطابقاً للخارج إحساناً للظن بالمتكلم؛ ويكون قد ظن أنه لم يفهمه لدقته عليه فلا يكون كذلك. هذا وقولهم في الحد الحقيقي: إنه متعسر، وإنه لا يقف عليه إلا آحاد الناس هو من الباب. فإن الحد الحقيقي إذا أريد به ما زعموه فإنه لا حقيقة له في الخارج، إذ يريدون به أن الموصوف في نفسه مؤلف من بعض صفاته اللازمة له التي بعضها أعم منه وبعضها مطابق له دون بعض صفاته اللازمة المساوية لتلك العامة في العموم وللمطابقة في المطابقة دون بعض، وأن حقيقته هي مركبة من تلك الصفات دون غيرها، وأن تلك الحقيقة يصورها الحد دون غيره. فهذا ليس بحق. فدعواهم تأليفه من بعض الصفات اللازمة دون بعض باطلة، بل دعواهم أنه مركب الصفات باطلة ودعواهم له حقيقة ثابتة في الخارج يصورها الحد دون غيره باطلة. وإنما الواقع أن المحدود الموصوف الذي ميز بالاسم أو الحد عن غيره قد يكون ثابتاً في الخارج، وقد يكون ثابتاً في المتكلم بالاسم أو الحد وهو يظن ثبوته في الخارج وليس كذلك. ولهذا يقال: الحد يكون تارة بحسب الاسم، وتارة بحسب المسمى. ويقال: الحد يكون تارة بحسب اسم الشيء، وتارة بحسب حقيقته. وإن كان الحد بحسب الاسم قد يكون مطابقاً للخارج، لكن المقصود أن الحد تارة يميز بين المراد باللفظ وغير المراد، وتارة يميز بين الموجود في الخارج من الأعيان وبين غيره؛ وهذا التمييز إنما يحصل بواسطة ذلك. فالتمييز الذي في النفس يجب أن يكون مطابقاً للتمييز في الخارج، والتمييز الذي يحصل للمستمع هو بواسطة التمييز الذي في نفس المتكلم، والله أعلم.
The matter of everyone who interprets the speech of a speaker or explains it: he may interpret the speaker's intended meaning and purpose, whether it corresponds to external reality or not, and it may become evident along with that that it corresponds to the external matter, and that it is true in itself. And if the speech is not true, it does not correspond to external reality, so the listener wants to make it correspond to reality, but it does not correspond nor agree, until someone may think that the explainer or listener did not understand the speaker's intended meaning due to its difficulty, but it is not so; rather, because the speech he mentioned is not corresponding to reality, so it cannot be made to correspond to it. And sometimes the one who thinks it corresponds to external reality does so out of good assumption of the speaker; and he may think that he did not understand it due to its subtlety, but it is not so. This, and their statement about real definition: that it is difficult, and that only a few people can attain it, is of this category. For real definition, if what they claim is intended, then it has no reality in external existence, because they intend by it that the described thing in itself is composed of some of its essential attributes, some of which are more general than it and some correspond to it, to the exclusion of some of its essential attributes that are equal to those general ones in generality and to the corresponding ones in correspondence, and that its reality is composed of those attributes to the exclusion of others, and that that reality is depicted by the definition alone. So this is not true. So their claim that it is composed of some essential attributes to the exclusion of others is false; rather, their claim that it is composed of attributes is false, and their claim that it has a fixed reality in external existence that the definition depicts to the exclusion of others is false. The reality is that the defined described thing that is distinguished by name or definition from others may be fixed in external existence, and may be fixed in the speaker's mind by name or definition, while he thinks it is fixed in external existence but it is not so. Hence it is said: definition is sometimes according to the name, and sometimes according to the named. And it is said: definition is sometimes according to the name of the thing, and sometimes according to its reality. Even if the definition according to the name may correspond to external reality, the point is that definition sometimes distinguishes between what is intended by the utterance and what is not intended, and sometimes distinguishes between the existing external entities and others; and this distinction is only achieved by means of that. So the distinction that is in the mind must correspond to the distinction in external existence, and the distinction that the listener obtains is by means of the distinction in the speaker's mind. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is a critical analysis of the logicians' concept of real definition (hadd haqiqi). Ibn Taymiyya begins by discussing the interpretation of speech: an interpreter may capture the speaker's intended meaning whether it corresponds to reality or not. If the speech is false, it cannot be made to correspond to reality. He then applies this to the logicians' claim that real definition is difficult and only attainable by a few. He argues that their notion of real definition—the thing composed of some essential attributes that are more general or equivalent, excluding others—has no basis in external reality. Their claim that the definition depicts a fixed essence is false. Instead, definition can be by name or by named, distinguishing meanings or external entities. The distinction in the mind must match external distinction. This passage guards against the misconception that real definition captures an objective essence independent of mental classification.

Key Terms
الحد الحقيقي (al-hadd al-haqiqi): Ibn Taymiyya denies its external reality, calling it a composition of some essential attributes that the logicians claim defines the essence but is arbitrary and false. [Note: No significant shift; Ibn Taymiyya is critiquing the standard logicians' concept.]
الحد بحسب الاسم (al-hadd bi-hasb al-ism): A definition that distinguishes the intended meaning of a term, which may or may not correspond to external reality. [Note: Stable across the tradition as a type of definition.]
الحد بحسب المسمى (al-hadd bi-hasb al-musamma): A definition that distinguishes the actual external entity, requiring correspondence to reality. [Note: Stable across the tradition.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the main problem with the logicians' real definition?
A) It is too difficult for most people to understand.
B) It arbitrarily selects some attributes and has no basis in external existence.
C) It only works for definitions by name, not by named.
D) It contradicts the concept of definition by name.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya dismantles the logicians' real definition by showing it is an arbitrary mental construction, and he replaces it with a distinction between definition by name and definition by named, emphasizing that mental distinctions must correspond to external reality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In a fiqh debate, two scholars define 'khamr' (wine). Scholar A says it is 'any intoxicating liquid made from grapes'. Scholar B says it is 'any intoxicating substance, regardless of source'. Using Ibn Taymiyya's distinction, analyse which type of definition (by name or by named) each is using, and evaluate whether they correspond to external reality.
?
Choose an Islamic legal term (e.g., 'salah', 'zakat') and construct both a definition by name (distinguishing its meaning in the Sharia) and a definition by named (distinguishing its instances in external acts). Explain how the two differ.

Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of Logical Definitions in Prophetic Sciences
Ibn Taymiyya criticizes mixing Greek logic with prophetic sciences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Ibn Taymiyya's critique of using logicians' definitions in prophetic sciences and explain the harms he attributes to this practice.

Core Idea
Mixing Greek logical definitions with revealed sciences corrupts both intellect and religion.

In this passage from his 'Radd 'ala al-Mantiqiyyin', Ibn Taymiyya launches a sharp critique against the practice of mixing the definitions (hudud) of Greek logic with the prophetic sciences. He argues that this mixture has led to corruption of intellects and religions, and that the logicians' definitions are not only useless but actually harmful. Let's unpack his key claims and understand why he considers this a dangerous deviation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target of the critique
Find the specific practice Ibn Taymiyya is criticizing. Look for the phrase 'mixing the articles of the people of logic with the prophetic sciences' (خلط مقالات أهل المنطق بالعلوم النبوية). This is his target.
2
Extract his central claim about definitions
Ibn Taymiyya states that the logicians' definitions (حدود المنطقيين) do not provide knowledge; they only waste time and cause confusion. He says they are 'false, combining differing things and separating similar ones.' Identify this claim in the Arabic.
He distinguishes between definitions that contain no falsehood (which he acknowledges) and the logicians' definitions, which he condemns.
3
List the specific harms he enumerates
The author lists several harmful consequences: wasting time, tiring minds, nonsense, false claims of verification, distraction from necessary matters, and establishing ignorance. Scan the text to find these.
These harms are explicitly mentioned after 'There is no benefit to that conventional [practice] except...'
4
Understand his historical reference
Ibn Taymiyya notes that early theologians (قدماء المتكلمين) did not approve of delving into logical definitions, and that this practice was introduced by later theologians who thought it was verification, but it is actually a deviation. This shows he sees it as a departure from the sound approach.
He contrasts the early approach (focused on evidences and rulings) with the later adoption of logical definitions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقام الثاني - بعض فوائد المنطق اليوناني ! خلط مقالات أهل المنطق بالعلوم النبوية وإفساد ذلك للعقول والأديان وقد تفطّن أبو عبد الله الرازي بنُ الخطيب لما عليه أئمة الكلام، وقرّر في محصله» وغيره أن التصورات لا تكون مكتسبة، وهذا هو حقيقة قول القائلين: «إن الحدّ لا يفيد تصوير المحدود». لكنه لم يهتذ هو وأمثاله إلى ما سبق إليه أئمة الكلام في هذا المقام . وهذا مقام شريف ينبغي أن يعرف فإنه بسبب إهماله دخل الفساد في العقول والأديان على كثير من الناس، إذ خلطوا ما ذكره أهلُ المنطق في «الحدود» بالعلوم النبوية التي جاءت بها الرسل - التي عند المسلمين واليهود والنصارى - بل وسائر العلوم، كالطب، والنحو، وغير ذلك . وصاروا يعظمون أمر «الحدود»، ويدعون أنهم هم المحققون لذلك، وأن ما ذكره غيرهم من الحدود إنما هي لفظية لا تفيد تعريف الماهية والحقيقة بخلاف حدودهم، ويسْلُكون الطرق الصعبة الطويلة والعبارات المتكلّفة الهائلة. وليس لذلك الاصطلاحي! فائدة إلا تضييع الزمان، وإتعاب الأذهان وكثرة الهذيان ودعوى التحقيق بالكذب والبهتان، وشَغل النفوس بما لا ينفعها - بل قد يُضلّها - عما لا بد لها منه ، وإثبات الجهل الذي هو أصلُ النفاق في القلوب، وإن ادعوا أنه أصلُ المعرفة والتحقيق . المنهى عنه وهذا من توابع الكلام الذي كان السلف ينهون عنه، وإن كان الذي نَهَوا عنه خيراً من هذا ،وأحسن إذ هو كلام في أدلّة وأحكام ولم يكن قدماء المتكلمين يرضون أن يخوضوا في «الحدود» على طريقة المنطقيين، كما دخل في ذلك متأخروهم الذين ظنوا ذلك من التحقيق، وإنما هو زيغ عن سواء الطريق . ولهذا لما كانت هذه الحدود» ونحوها لا تفيد الإنسان علماً لم يكن عنده، وإنما تفيده كثرة كلام، سموهم «أهل الكلام». وهذا - لَعَمْري - في الحدود» التي ليس فيها باطل . فأما حدود المنطقيين» التي يدعون أنهم يصوّرون بها الحقائق فإنها باطلة، يجمعون بها بين المختلفين ويفرقون بين المتماثلين.
The second station: Some benefits of Greek logic! Mixing the articles of the people of logic with the prophetic sciences and its corruption of intellects and religions. Abu Abdullah al-Razi ibn al-Khatib perceived what the imams of kalam were upon, and established in his 'Muhassal' and elsewhere that conceptualizations (tasawwurat) are not acquired, and this is the reality of the saying of those who say: 'The definition does not give a mental picture of the defined.' But he and his likes did not reach what the imams of kalam preceded to in this station. And this is a noble station that should be known, for because of its neglect, corruption entered into intellects and religions for many people, since they mixed what the people of logic mentioned about 'definitions' with the prophetic sciences brought by the messengers - which are with the Muslims, Jews, and Christians - rather, with all [other] sciences, such as medicine, grammar, and others. And they began to magnify the matter of 'definitions', claiming that they are the verifiers of that, and that what others mention of definitions are merely verbal, not giving definition of essence and reality, unlike their definitions. And they take difficult, lengthy paths and elaborate, strained expressions. And there is no benefit to that conventional [practice] except wasting time, tiring minds, much nonsense, claiming verification with lies and slander, and occupying souls with what does not benefit them - rather, may lead them astray - from what is necessary for them, and establishing ignorance which is the root of hypocrisy in hearts, even if they claim it is the root of knowledge and verification. [This is] what is forbidden. And this is from the consequences of the speech that the predecessors used to forbid; although what they forbade was better than this, and more excellent, for it is speech about evidences and rulings. And the early theologians were not satisfied to delve into 'definitions' in the manner of the logicians, as their later ones who thought that to be verification entered into that, but it is a deviation from the straight path. And because of this, when these 'definitions' and the like do not give a person knowledge he did not have, but rather give him much talk, they called them 'people of kalam'. And this - by my life - applies to definitions that contain no falsehood. As for the definitions of the logicians, which they claim to picture realities by, they are false; they combine differing things and separate similar ones.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is a critique by Ibn Taymiyya of the logicians' practice of mixing their definitions (hudud) with the prophetic sciences. He begins by stating the second station of his work, which concerns some 'benefits' of Greek logic, using irony. He mentions that al-Razi realized that conceptualizations are not acquired, aligning with those who say definitions do not give knowledge. However, al-Razi did not grasp the full import of the earlier theologians' position. Ibn Taymiyya then emphasizes that neglecting this principle has corrupted intellects and religions, as people have mixed logical definitions with revealed sciences, even with secular sciences like medicine and grammar. The logicians magnify their definitions, claiming theirs are real while others' are merely verbal. They take long-winded approaches, but the only outcome is wasted time, mental fatigue, nonsense, false claims, and distraction from what is necessary. He traces this to the speech (kalam) that the pious predecessors forbade, noting that even the early mutakallimun avoided these logical definitions. He concludes that the logicians' definitions are false, as they conflate distinct things and separate similar ones, which is the opposite of true definition.

Key Terms
الحدود
المنطق
العلوم النبوية

Ibn Taymiyya's Refutation of Definitions as Knowledge Sources
Ibn Taymiyya presents his first evidence that definitions (hudud) do not provide knowledge of the defined.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's first argument that definitions (hudud) do not provide knowledge and evaluate its internal validity.

Core Idea
A definition is just a claim; without evidence, it cannot give new knowledge.

Ibn Taymiyya launches a direct attack on the foundational claim of Aristotelian logic: that definitions (hudud) provide a mental picture of essences. In this passage, he offers a simple but devastating argument: a definition is nothing but the definer's assertion, and a bare assertion cannot generate knowledge. Let's walk through his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim being attacked
Logicians claim definitions give knowledge of the defined (taswir al-mahdud). Ibn Taymiyya states that the definition is merely the definer's statement and claim.
The term 'hadd' here refers to any definition, whether a complete sentence or a qualified term.
2
Characterize Ibn Taymiyya's view of a definition
He says a definition is a declarative proposition (qadiyya khabariyya) and a mere claim devoid of proof (hujja).
Example: defining 'human' as 'rational animal' is a claim, not a proof.
3
Follow the dilemma
Either the listener already knows that the defined has that property, in which case the definition gives no new knowledge; or they do not know it, in which case they have no reason to trust the definer, who is not infallible.
This is a classic epistemological dilemma.
4
Conclude the argument
In both cases, the definition does not provide new knowledge. The definition is redundant if known, and unsubstantiated if unknown.
Ibn Taymiyya also addresses the objection that definitions might be simple terms, but he responds that a simple term also does not benefit without evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأدلة على بطلان دعواهم أن الحدود تفيد تصوير الحقائق ونحن نبيّن أن الحدود لا تفيد تصوير الحقائق، وأن حدود أهل المنطق التي يسمونها «حقيقية» تُفسد العقل . والدليل على ذلك وجوه : . الوجه الأول الحد - سواءٌ جُعل مركباً أو مفرداً - لا يفيد معرفة المحدود أحدها : إن الحدّ مجرّد قول الحادّ ودعواه، فإنه إذا قال: حدّ «الإنسان» مثلاً : «إنه حيوان الناطق أو الضاحك»، فهذه قضيّة خبرية، ومجرّد دعوى خليّة عن حجّة . فإما أن يكون المستمع لها عالماً يصدقها بدون هذا القول وإما أن لا يكون. فإن كان عالماً بذلك ثبت أنه لم يستفد هذه المعرفة بهذا الحد، وإن لم يكن عالماً، يصدّقه بمجرد قول المخبر الذي لا دليل معه لا يفيده العلم كيف وهو يعلم أنه ليس بمعصوم في قوله (۱)؟ فقد تبين أنه على التقديرين ليس الحدّ هو الذي يفيده معرفة المحدود. فإن قيل : الحدّ ليس هو الجملة الخبرية، وإنما هو مجرّد قولك حيوان ناطق، غير مفيد [۲۸] وهذا مفرد لا جملة - وهذا السؤال وارد على أحد اصطلاحيهم؛ فإنهم تارة يجعلون الحد هو الجملة التامة كما يقوله الغزالي وغيره، وتارة يجعلون الحد هو المفرد المقيَّد كالاسم وهو الذي يسمونه «التركيب» التقييدي، كما يذكر ذلك الرازي ونحوه - قيل : التكلم بالمفرد لا يفيد ولا يكون جواباً لسائل، سواء كان موصوفا مركباً تركيباً تقييدياً أو لم يكن كذلك .
The proofs of the falsity of their claim that definitions give a mental picture of realities. And we will show that definitions do not give a mental picture of realities, and that the definitions of the logicians, which they call 'real', corrupt the intellect. The proof of that is through aspects: The first aspect: The definition - whether made compound or simple - does not give knowledge of the defined. One of them: That the definition is merely the statement of the definer and his claim. For if he says, defining 'human' for example: 'It is a rational animal' or 'a laughing animal', then this is a declarative statement, a mere claim devoid of proof. So either the listener is knowledgeable, accepting it without this statement, or he is not. If he is knowledgeable of that, then it is established that he did not benefit this knowledge from this definition; if he is not knowledgeable, then his believing the mere statement of an informant who has no evidence with him does not give him knowledge - how, when he knows that he is not infallible in his statement? So it is clear that in both cases, it is not the definition that gives him knowledge of the defined. If it is said: The definition is not a declarative sentence; rather it is just your saying 'rational animal', not a complete sentence, and this is a simple term, not a sentence - and this question occurs according to one of their terminologies; for sometimes they make the definition a complete sentence as al-Ghazali and others say, and sometimes they make the definition a qualified simple term like a name, which they call 'attributive composition', as al-Razi and the like mention - then it is said: Speaking with a simple term does not benefit and does not constitute an answer to a questioner, whether it is described as compound by attributive composition or not.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage presents Ibn Taymiyya's first argument against the logicians' claim that definitions (hudud) provide knowledge of the defined (taswir al-mahdud). He begins by stating that definitions do not give a mental picture of realities, and the logicians' 'real' definitions actually corrupt the intellect. Then he gives the first proof: a definition is merely the definer's statement and claim. For example, if one defines 'human' as 'rational animal', this is a declarative proposition (qadiyya khabariyya) and a mere claim without evidence. The listener either already knows this (in which case the definition gives no new knowledge) or does not know it (in which case he has no reason to trust the definer, who is not infallible). Thus, in either case, the definition does not give knowledge. Ibn Taymiyya then addresses an objection: some logicians (like al-Ghazali) say the definition is a complete sentence, while others (like al-Razi) say it is a qualified simple term (like 'rational animal' as a compound term). He responds that speaking with a simple term still does not benefit the questioner, whether it is a qualified compound or not. The key point is that the definition, as a mere claim, cannot be a source of new knowledge without evidence.

Key Terms
الحد
القضية الخبرية
التركيب التقييدي

C) Because the definer is always lying.
D) Because definitions are only verbal.

Key Takeaway
A definition, being a mere declarative claim without proof, cannot provide new knowledge about the defined object.
